<div class="description"></div></div></div></div>
</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Concertos" title="Brandenburg Concertos">Brandenburg Concertos</a></div>
<p>Bach's best-known orchestral works are the <i>Brandenburg Concertos</i>, so named because he submitted them in the hope of gaining employment from <a href="/wiki/Margrave_Christian_Ludwig_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt" title="Margrave Christian Ludwig of Brandenburg-Schwedt">Margrave Christian Ludwig of Brandenburg-Schwedt</a> in 1721; his application was unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_25-8"><a href="#cite_note-Baroquenet-25">[22]</a></sup> These works are examples of the <a href="/wiki/Concerto_grosso" title="Concerto grosso">concerto grosso</a> genre.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Keyboard_concertos">Keyboard concertos</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_concertos_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Keyboard concertos by Johann Sebastian Bach">Keyboard concertos by Johann Sebastian Bach</a></div>
<p>Bach composed and transcribed concertos for one to four harpsichords. Many of the harpsichord concertos were not original works but arrangements of his concertos for other instruments, now lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[170]</a></sup> A number of violin, oboe, and flute concertos have been reconstructed from these.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orchestral_suites">Orchestral suites</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Orchestral_suites_(Bach)" title="Orchestral suites (Bach)">Orchestral suites (Bach)</a></div>
<p>In addition to concertos, Bach wrote four <a href="/wiki/Orchestral_suites_(Bach)" title="Orchestral suites (Bach)">orchestral suites</a>, each suite being a series of stylised dances for orchestra, preceded by a <a href="/wiki/French_overture" title="French overture">French overture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Copies.2C_arrangements_and_uncertain_attributions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Copies,_arrangements_and_uncertain_attributions">Copies, arrangements and uncertain attributions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097025294" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096940132" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><div class="listen-header">Some of Bach's most popular melodies are, more often than not, heard in various arrangements:</div>
<div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_naxos_8.550194_01_13.ogg" title="File:Wiki naxos 8.550194 01 13.ogg"><i>Air on the G String</i> (excerpt)</a></div>
<div><audio controls="" data-durationhint="170" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Wiki_naxos_8.550194_01_13.ogg" id="mwe_player_34" preload="none" style="width:232px;" width="232"><source data-bandwidth="125507" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (126 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Wiki_naxos_8.550194_01_13.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="198736" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/ba/Wiki_naxos_8.550194_01_13.ogg/Wiki_naxos_8.550194_01_13.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio></div>
<div class="description">"Air", 2nd movement from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BWV_1068" title="BWV 1068">Orchestral Suite No. 3 in D major, BWV 1068</a>, performed in an <i><a href="/wiki/Air_on_the_G_String" title="Air on the G String">Air on the G String</a></i> adaptation by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capella_Istropolitana" title="Capella Istropolitana">Capella Istropolitana</a> conducted by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_von_Dohn%C3%A1nyi" title="Oliver von Dohnányi">Oliver von Dohnányi</a> (courtesy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naxos_Records" title="Naxos Records">Naxos</a>)</div></div><hr/><div class="haudio">
<div class="listen-file-header"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheep_May_Safely_Graze_BWV_208.ogg" title="File:Sheep May Safely Graze BWV 208.ogg">"Sheep May Safely Graze" (instrumental version)</a></div>
<div><audio controls="" data-durationhint="238" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Sheep_May_Safely_Graze_BWV_208.ogg" id="mwe_player_35" preload="none" style="width:232px;" width="232"><source data-bandwidth="102944" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (103 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Sheep_May_Safely_Graze_BWV_208.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="186704" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/c/c4/Sheep_May_Safely_Graze_BWV_208.ogg/Sheep_May_Safely_Graze_BWV_208.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/></audio></div>
<div class="description">The aria "Schafe können sicher weiden" (Sheep May Safely Graze), No. 9 from the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunting_Cantata" title="Hunting Cantata">Hunting Cantata</a></i>, BWV 208: composed for soprano, recorders, and continuo, the music of this movement exists in a variety of instrumental arrangements.</div></div></div></div>
</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/BWV_Anh." title="BWV Anh.">BWV Anh.</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcriptions_of_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="List of transcriptions of compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach">List of transcriptions of compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach</a></div>
<p>In his early youth, Bach copied pieces by other composers to learn from them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen49mode2up_10–11]_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen49mode2up_10–11]-175">[172]</a></sup> Later, he copied and arranged music for performance or as study material for his pupils. Some of these pieces, like "<a href="/wiki/Bist_du_bei_mir" title="Bist du bei mir">Bist du bei mir</a>" (copied not by Bach but by Anna Magdalena), became famous before being dissociated with Bach. Bach copied and arranged Italian masters such as Vivaldi (e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BWV_1065" title="BWV 1065">BWV 1065</a>), <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Pergolesi" title="Giovanni Battista Pergolesi">Pergolesi</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BWV_1083" title="BWV 1083">BWV 1083</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Pierluigi_da_Palestrina" title="Giovanni Pierluigi da Palestrina">Palestrina</a> (<a class="extiw" href="https://imslp.org/wiki/Missa_Sine_nomine_(Palestrina,_Giovanni_Pierluigi_da)#Arrangements_and_Transcriptions" title="scores:Missa Sine nomine (Palestrina, Giovanni Pierluigi da)">Missa Sine nomine</a>), French masters such as <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Couperin" title="François Couperin">François Couperin</a> (<a href="/wiki/Notebook_for_Anna_Magdalena_Bach#The_1725_notebook" title="Notebook for Anna Magdalena Bach">BWV Anh. 183</a>), and, closer to home, various German masters including Telemann (e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_solo_keyboard_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach#Miscellaneous_suites_(818–824)" title="List of solo keyboard compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach">BWV 824</a>=<a class="extiw" href="https://imslp.org/wiki/Suite_in_A_major,_TWV_32:14_(Telemann,_Georg_Philipp)" title="scores:Suite in A major, TWV 32:14 (Telemann, Georg Philipp)">TWV 32:14</a>) and Handel (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Mark_Passion_pastiche#Leipzig_1747–1748_(BC_D_5)" title="St Mark Passion pastiche">arias from <i>Brockes Passion</i></a>), and music from members of his own family. He also often copied and arranged his own music (e.g. movements from cantatas for his short masses <a href="/wiki/Kyrie%E2%80%93Gloria_masses,_BWV_233%E2%80%93236" title="Kyrie–Gloria masses, BWV 233–236">BWV 233–236</a>), as his music was likewise copied and arranged by others. Some of these arrangements, like the late 19th-century "<a href="/wiki/Air_on_the_G_String" title="Air on the G String">Air on the G String</a>", helped to popularise Bach's music.
</p><p>Sometimes "who copied whom" is not clear. For instance, Forkel mentions a Mass for double chorus among the works composed by Bach. The work was published and performed in the early 19th century, and although a score partially in Bach's handwriting exists, the work was later considered spurious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen187mode2up_140–141]_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen187mode2up_140–141]-176">[173]</a></sup> In 1950, the design of the Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis was to keep such works out of the main catalogue: if there was a strong association with Bach they could be listed in its appendix (German: <i>Anhang</i>, abbreviated as Anh.). Thus, for instance, the aforementioned Mass for double chorus became <a href="/wiki/Bach%27s_church_music_in_Latin#Copies" title="Bach's church music in Latin">BWV Anh. 167</a>. But this was far from the end of the attribution issues. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Schlage_doch,_gew%C3%BCnschte_Stunde,_BWV_53" title="Schlage doch, gewünschte Stunde, BWV 53"><i>Schlage doch, gewünschte Stunde</i>, BWV 53</a>, was later attributed to <a href="/wiki/Melchior_Hoffmann_(composer)" title="Melchior Hoffmann (composer)">Melchior Hoffmann</a>. For other works, Bach's authorship was put in doubt without a generally accepted answer to the question of whether or not he composed it: the best known organ composition in the BWV catalogue, the <a href="/wiki/Toccata_and_Fugue_in_D_minor,_BWV_565" title="Toccata and Fugue in D minor, BWV 565">Toccata and Fugue in D minor, BWV 565</a>, was indicated as one of these uncertain works in the late 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reception_of_Johann_Sebastian_Bach%27s_music" title="Reception of Johann Sebastian Bach's music">Reception of Johann Sebastian Bach's music</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Johann_Sebastian_Bach&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Johann+Sebastian+Bach%22" rel="nofollow">"Johann Sebastian Bach"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Johann+Sebastian+Bach%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Johann+Sebastian+Bach%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Johann+Sebastian+Bach%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Johann+Sebastian+Bach%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Johann+Sebastian+Bach%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2769" data-file-width="2588" decoding="async" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg/220px-Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg/330px-Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg/440px-Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The church in Arnstadt where Bach had been the organist from 1703 to 1707. In 1935 the church was renamed "Bachkirche".</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout the 18th century, the appreciation of Bach's music was mostly limited to distinguished connoisseurs. The 19th century started with publication of the first biography of the composer and ended with the completion of the publication of all of Bach's known works by the <a href="/wiki/Bach_Gesellschaft" title="Bach Gesellschaft">Bach Gesellschaft</a>. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bach_Revival" title="Bach Revival">Bach Revival</a> had started from <a href="/wiki/Felix_Mendelssohn" title="Felix Mendelssohn">Mendelssohn</a>'s performance of the <i><a href="/wiki/St_Matthew_Passion" title="St Matthew Passion">St Matthew Passion</a></i> in 1829. Soon after that performance, Bach started to become regarded as one of the greatest composers of all time, if not the greatest, a reputation he has retained ever since. A new extensive Bach biography was published in the second half of the 19th century.
</p><p>In the 20th century Bach's music was widely performed and recorded, while the <a href="/wiki/Neue_Bachgesellschaft" title="Neue Bachgesellschaft">Neue Bachgesellschaft</a>, among others, published research on the composer. Modern adaptations of Bach's music contributed greatly to his popularisation in the second half of the 20th century. Among these were the <a href="/wiki/The_Swingle_Singers" title="The Swingle Singers">Swingle Singers</a>' versions of Bach pieces (for instance, the <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">Air</i></span> from <a href="/wiki/Orchestral_suites_(Bach)#Suite_No._3_in_D_major,_BWV_1068" title="Orchestral suites (Bach)">Orchestral Suite No. 3</a>, and the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Wachet auf...</i></span> chorale prelude) and <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Carlos" title="Wendy Carlos">Wendy Carlos</a>' 1968 <i><a href="/wiki/Switched-On_Bach" title="Switched-On Bach">Switched-On Bach</a></i>, which used the <a href="/wiki/Moog_synthesizer" title="Moog synthesizer">Moog electronic synthesiser</a>.
</p><p>By the end of the 20th century, more classical performers were gradually moving away from the performance style and instrumentation that were established in the romantic era: they started to perform Bach's music on <a href="/wiki/List_of_period_instruments#Baroque_(1600–1750)" title="List of period instruments">period instruments of the baroque era</a>, studied and practised playing techniques and tempi as established in his time, and reduced the size of instrumental ensembles and choirs to what he would have employed. The <a href="/wiki/BACH_motif" title="BACH motif">BACH motif</a>, used by the composer in his own compositions, was used in dozens of tributes to the composer from the 19th century to the 21st. In the 21st century the complete extant output of the composer became available online, with several websites exclusively dedicated to him.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Calendar_of_saints_(Episcopal_Church)" title="Calendar of saints (Episcopal Church)">liturgical calendar of the Episcopal Church</a> remembers Bach annually with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feast_day" title="Feast day">feast day</a> on 28 July<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> on the same day, the <a href="/wiki/Calendar_of_saints_(Lutheran)" title="Calendar of saints (Lutheran)">Calendar of Saints</a> of some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran_church" title="Lutheran church">Lutheran churches</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">ELCA</a>, remembers Bach and Handel with <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Sch%C3%BCtz" title="Heinrich Schütz">Heinrich Schütz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27,_vor_1798.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3152" data-file-width="2457" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg/220px-17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg/330px-17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg/440px-17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27,_vor_1798.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Painting of Johann Sebastian Bach by 'Gebel', before 1798.</div></div></div>
<p>In his own time, Bach was highly regarded amongst his colleagues,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeck2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidN1zSVDYTCXgCpgPA141_141]_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeck2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidN1zSVDYTCXgCpgPA141_141]-180">[177]</a></sup> although his reputation outside of this small circle of connoisseurs was due not to his compositions (which had an extremely narrow circulation),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolffEmery2001_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolffEmery2001-13">[11]</a></sup> but due to his virtuosic abilities. Nevertheless, during his life, Bach received public recognition, such as the title of court composer by <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland" title="Augustus III of Poland">Augustus III of Poland</a> and the appreciation he was shown by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Karl_von_Keyserling" title="Hermann Karl von Keyserling">Hermann Karl von Keyserling</a>. Such highly placed appreciation contrasted with the humiliations he had to cope with, for instance in Leipzig.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup> Also in the contemporary press, Bach had his detractors, such as <a href="/wiki/Johann_Adolf_Scheibe" title="Johann Adolf Scheibe">Johann Adolf Scheibe</a>, suggesting he write less complex music, and his supporters, such as <a href="/wiki/Johann_Mattheson" title="Johann Mattheson">Johann Mattheson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_Christoph_Mizler" title="Lorenz Christoph Mizler">Lorenz Christoph Mizler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup>
</p><p>After his death, Bach's reputation as a composer at first declined: his work was regarded as old-fashioned compared to the emerging <a href="/wiki/Galant_music" title="Galant music">galant</a> style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup> Initially, he was remembered more as a virtuoso player of the organ and as a teacher. The bulk of the music that had been <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach_printed_during_his_lifetime" title="List of compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach printed during his lifetime">printed during the composer's lifetime</a>, at least the part that was remembered, was for the organ and the harpsichord. Thus, his reputation as a composer was initially mostly limited to his keyboard music, and that even fairly limited to its value in music education.
</p><p>Bach's surviving family members, who inherited a large part of his manuscripts, were not all equally concerned with preserving them, leading to considerable losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff2000456–461_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2000456–461-186">[183]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carl_Philipp_Emanuel_Bach" title="Carl Philipp Emanuel Bach">Carl Philipp Emanuel</a>, his second eldest son, was most active in safeguarding his father's legacy: he co-authored his father's obituary, contributed to the publication of his four-part chorales,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen130mode1up_85–86]_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen130mode1up_85–86]-187">[184]</a></sup> staged some of his works, and the bulk of previously unpublished works of his father were preserved with his help.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Friedemann_Bach" title="Wilhelm Friedemann Bach">Wilhelm Friedemann</a>, the eldest son, performed several of his father's cantatas in <a href="/wiki/Halle_(Saale)" title="Halle (Saale)">Halle</a> but after becoming unemployed sold part of the large collection of his father's works he owned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen186mode1up_139]_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen186mode1up_139]-190">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff2013459_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2013459-191">[188]</a></sup> Several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_students_of_Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="List of students of Johann Sebastian Bach">students of the old master</a>, such as his son-in-law <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christoph_Altnickol" title="Johann Christoph Altnickol">Johann Christoph Altnickol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Friedrich_Agricola" title="Johann Friedrich Agricola">Johann Friedrich Agricola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Kirnberger" title="Johann Kirnberger">Johann Kirnberger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johann_Ludwig_Krebs" title="Johann Ludwig Krebs">Johann Ludwig Krebs</a>, contributed to the dissemination of his legacy. The early devotees were not all musicians; for example, in Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Itzig" title="Daniel Itzig">Daniel Itzig</a>, a high official of Frederick the Great's court, venerated Bach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[189]</a></sup> His eldest daughters took lessons from Kirnberger and their sister Sara from <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Friedemann_Bach" title="Wilhelm Friedemann Bach">Wilhelm Friedemann Bach</a>, who was in Berlin from 1774 to 1784.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apple14_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Apple14-193">[190]</a></sup> Sara Itzig Levy became an avid collector of works by Johann Sebastian Bach and his sons and was a "patron" of CPE Bach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apple14_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-Apple14-193">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>While in Leipzig, performances of Bach's church music were limited to some of his motets, and under <a href="/wiki/Thomaskantor" title="Thomaskantor">cantor</a> <a href="/wiki/Johann_Friedrich_Doles" title="Johann Friedrich Doles">Doles</a> some of his <a href="/wiki/Passions_(Bach)" title="Passions (Bach)">Passions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitta1899b[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage518mode2up_518–519],_[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage611mode1up_611]_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitta1899b[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage518mode2up_518–519],_[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage611mode1up_611]-194">[191]</a></sup> A new generation of Bach aficionados emerged: they studiously collected and copied his music, including some of his large-scale works such as the <a href="/wiki/Mass_in_B_minor" title="Mass in B minor">Mass in B minor</a> and performed it privately. One such connoisseur was <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_van_Swieten" title="Gottfried van Swieten">Gottfried van Swieten</a>, a high-ranking Austrian official who was instrumental in passing Bach's legacy on to the composers of the <a href="/wiki/First_Viennese_School" title="First Viennese School">Viennese school</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Haydn</a> owned manuscript copies of the <i>Well-Tempered Clavier</i> and the Mass in B minor and was influenced by Bach's music. <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a> owned a copy of one of Bach's motets,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[192]</a></sup> transcribed some of his instrumental works (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=K._404a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="K. 404a (page does not exist)">K. 404a</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=K._405&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="K. 405 (page does not exist)">405</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[194]</a></sup> and wrote contrapuntal music influenced by his style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apbrown_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-apbrown-199">[196]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Beethoven</a> played the entire <i>Well-Tempered Clavier</i> by the time he was 11 and described Bach as <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Urvater der Harmonie</i></span> (progenitor of harmony).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-McKay-200">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schenk1959p101_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schenk1959p101-201">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerst1904101_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerst1904101-203">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[201]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Altes_Bachdenkmal_(Leipzig)_-_Holzstich.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2525" data-file-width="1801" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg/170px-Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg/255px-Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg/340px-Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Altes_Bachdenkmal_(Leipzig)_-_Holzstich.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Image of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=19th_century_Bach_memorial_(Leipzig)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="19th century Bach memorial (Leipzig) (page does not exist)">Bach memorial</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altes_Bach-Denkmal_in_Leipzig" title="de:Altes Bach-Denkmal in Leipzig">de</a>]</span> erected by Felix Mendelssohn in Leipzig in 1843</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bach_Revival" title="Bach Revival">Bach Revival</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Matthew_Passion#19th_century" title="St Matthew Passion">St Matthew Passion § 19th century</a></div>
<p>In 1802, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Nikolaus_Forkel" title="Johann Nikolaus Forkel">Johann Nikolaus Forkel</a> published <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ueber_Johann_Sebastian_Bachs_Leben,_Kunst_und_Kunstwerke" title="Ueber Johann Sebastian Bachs Leben, Kunst und Kunstwerke">Ueber Johann Sebastian Bachs Leben, Kunst und Kunstwerke</a></i>, the first biography of the composer, which contributed to his becoming known to a wider public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeck20069–10_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeck20069–10-205">[202]</a></sup> In 1805, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham_Mendelssohn" title="Abraham Mendelssohn">Abraham Mendelssohn</a>, who had married one of Itzig's granddaughters, bought a substantial collection of Bach manuscripts that had come down from C. P. E. Bach, and donated it to the <a href="/wiki/Sing-Akademie_zu_Berlin" title="Sing-Akademie zu Berlin">Berlin Sing-Akademie</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[189]</a></sup> The Sing-Akademie occasionally performed Bach's works in public concerts, for instance his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BWV_1052" title="BWV 1052">first keyboard concerto</a>, with Sara Itzig Levy at the piano.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-3"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[189]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first decades of the 19th century saw an increasing number of first publications of Bach's music: Breitkopf started publishing chorale preludes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen99mode1up_94]_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen99mode1up_94]-206">[203]</a></sup> Hoffmeister harpsichord music,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen101mode1up_96–97]_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen101mode1up_96–97]-207">[204]</a></sup> and the <i>Well-Tempered Clavier</i> was printed concurrently by Simrock (Germany), Nägeli (Switzerland) and Hoffmeister (Germany and Austria) in 1801.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen105mode1up_100]_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen105mode1up_100]-208">[205]</a></sup> Vocal music was also published: motets in 1802 and 1803, followed by the E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">♭</span></span> major version of the <i><a href="/wiki/Magnificat_(Bach)" title="Magnificat (Bach)">Magnificat</a></i>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BWV_234" title="BWV 234">Kyrie-Gloria Mass in A major</a>, and the cantata <a href="/wiki/Ein_feste_Burg_ist_unser_Gott,_BWV_80" title="Ein feste Burg ist unser Gott, BWV 80"><i>Ein feste Burg ist unser Gott</i> (BWV 80)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen22mode1up_xvii]_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen22mode1up_xvii]-209">[206]</a></sup> In 1818, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Georg_N%C3%A4geli" title="Hans Georg Nägeli">Hans Georg Nägeli</a> called the <i>Mass in B minor</i> the greatest composition ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-McKay-200">[197]</a></sup> Bach's influence was felt in the next generation of early Romantic composers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schenk1959p101_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schenk1959p101-201">[198]</a></sup> When Felix Mendelssohn, Abraham's son, aged 13, produced his first <i>Magnificat</i> setting in 1822, it is clear that he had been inspired by the then unpublished D major version of Bach's <i>Magnificat</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>Felix Mendelssohn significantly contributed to the renewed interest in Bach's work with his 1829 Berlin performance of the <i><a href="/wiki/St_Matthew_Passion" title="St Matthew Passion">St Matthew Passion</a></i>, which was instrumental in setting off what has been called the Bach Revival. The <i><a href="/wiki/St_John_Passion" title="St John Passion">St John Passion</a></i> saw its 19th-century premiere in 1833, and the first performance of the <i>Mass in B minor</i> followed in 1844. Besides these and other public performances and an increased coverage on the composer and his compositions in printed media, the 1830s and 1840s also saw the first publication of more vocal works by Bach: six cantatas, the <i>St Matthew Passion</i>, and the <i>Mass in B minor</i>. A series of organ compositions saw their first publication in 1833.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[208]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Chopin</a> started composing his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/24_Preludes,_Op._28_(Chopin)" title="24 Preludes, Op. 28 (Chopin)">24 Preludes, Op. 28</a>, inspired by the <i>Well-Tempered Clavier</i>, in 1835, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schumann" title="Robert Schumann">Schumann</a> published his <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sechs_Fugen_%C3%BCber_den_Namen_B-A-C-H&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sechs Fugen über den Namen B-A-C-H (page does not exist)">Sechs Fugen über den Namen B-A-C-H</a></i> in 1845. Bach's music was transcribed and arranged to suit contemporary tastes and performance practice by composers such as <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Zelter" title="Carl Friedrich Zelter">Carl Friedrich Zelter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Franz" title="Robert Franz">Robert Franz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a>, or combined with new music such as the melody line of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Gounod" title="Charles Gounod">Charles Gounod</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Ave_Maria_(Bach/Gounod)" title="Ave Maria (Bach/Gounod)">Ave Maria</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay_200-2"><a href="#cite_note-McKay-200">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKupferberg1985126_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKupferberg1985126-212">[209]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Brahms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Bruckner" title="Anton Bruckner">Bruckner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Wagner</a> were among the composers who promoted Bach's music or wrote glowingly about it.
</p><p>In 1850, the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Bach_Gesellschaft" title="Bach Gesellschaft">Bach-Gesellschaft</a></i></span> (Bach Society) was founded to promote Bach's music. In the second half of the 19th century, the Society published a comprehensive edition of the composer's works. Also in the second half of the 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Spitta" title="Philipp Spitta">Philipp Spitta</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/Spitta%27s_Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Spitta's Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a></i>, the standard work on Bach's life and music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[210]</a></sup> By that time, Bach was known as the first of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Bs" title="Three Bs">three Bs</a> in music. Throughout the 19th century, 200 books were published on Bach. By the end of the century, local Bach societies were established in several cities, and his music had been performed in all major musical centres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay_200-3"><a href="#cite_note-McKay-200">[197]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Germany all throughout the century, Bach was coupled to nationalist feelings, and the composer was inscribed in a religious revival. In England, Bach was coupled to an existing revival of religious and baroque music. By the end of the century, Bach was firmly established as one of the greatest composers, recognised for both his instrumental and his vocal music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay_200-4"><a href="#cite_note-McKay-200">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2608" data-file-width="1952" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg/170px-Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg/255px-Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg/340px-Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1908 Statue of Bach in front of the Thomaskirche in Leipzig</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="522" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg/170px-Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg/255px-Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg/340px-Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>28 July 1950: memorial service for Bach in Leipzig's Thomaskirche, on the 200th anniversary of the composer's death</div></div></div>
<p>During the 20th century, the process of recognising the musical as well as the <a href="/wiki/Pedagogy" title="Pedagogy">pedagogic</a> value of some of the works continued, as in the promotion of the <a href="/wiki/Cello_Suites_(Bach)" title="Cello Suites (Bach)">cello suites</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Casals" title="Pablo Casals">Pablo Casals</a>, the first major performer to record these suites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[211]</a></sup> Leading performers of classical music such as <a href="/wiki/Willem_Mengelberg" title="Willem Mengelberg">Willem Mengelberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Fischer" title="Edwin Fischer">Edwin Fischer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georges_Enescu" title="Georges Enescu">Georges Enescu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Stokowski" title="Leopold Stokowski">Leopold Stokowski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_von_Karajan" title="Herbert von Karajan">Herbert von Karajan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Grumiaux" title="Arthur Grumiaux">Arthur Grumiaux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Walcha" title="Helmut Walcha">Helmut Walcha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wanda_Landowska" title="Wanda Landowska">Wanda Landowska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Richter_(conductor)" title="Karl Richter (conductor)">Karl Richter</a>, <a href="/wiki/I_Musici" title="I Musici">I Musici</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Fischer-Dieskau" title="Dietrich Fischer-Dieskau">Dietrich Fischer-Dieskau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Gould" title="Glenn Gould">Glenn Gould</a> recorded his music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[n 4]</a></sup>
</p><p>A significant development in the later part of the 20th century was the momentum gained by the <a href="/wiki/Historically_informed_performance" title="Historically informed performance">historically informed performance</a> practice, with forerunners such as <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Harnoncourt" title="Nikolaus Harnoncourt">Nikolaus Harnoncourt</a> acquiring prominence by their performances of Bach's music. His keyboard music was again performed more on the instruments Bach was familiar with, rather than on modern pianos and 19th-century romantic organs. Ensembles playing and singing Bach's music not only kept to the instruments and the performance style of his day but were also reduced to the size of the groups Bach used for his performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[212]</a></sup> But that was far from the only way Bach's music came to the forefront in the 20th century: his music was heard in versions ranging from <a href="/wiki/Ferruccio_Busoni" title="Ferruccio Busoni">Ferruccio Busoni</a>'s late romantic <a href="/wiki/Bach-Busoni_Editions" title="Bach-Busoni Editions">piano transcriptions</a> to jazzy interpretations such as those by <a href="/wiki/The_Swingle_Singers" title="The Swingle Singers">The Swingle Singers</a>, orchestrations like the one opening <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney" title="Walt Disney">Walt Disney</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Fantasia_(1940_film)" title="Fantasia (1940 film)">Fantasia</a></i> movie, and synthesiser performances such as <a href="/wiki/Wendy_Carlos" title="Wendy Carlos">Wendy Carlos</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Switched-On_Bach" title="Switched-On Bach">Switched-On Bach</a></i> recordings.
</p><p>Bach's music has influenced other genres. For instance, jazz musicians have adopted Bach's music, with <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Loussier" title="Jacques Loussier">Jacques Loussier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Anderson" title="Ian Anderson">Ian Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uri_Caine" title="Uri Caine">Uri Caine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Modern_Jazz_Quartet" title="Modern Jazz Quartet">Modern Jazz Quartet</a> among those creating jazz versions of his works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[213]</a></sup> Several 20th-century composers referred to Bach or his music, for example <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Ysa%C3%BFe" title="Eugène Ysaÿe">Eugène Ysaÿe</a> in <a href="/wiki/Six_Sonatas_for_solo_violin_(Ysa%C3%BFe)" title="Six Sonatas for solo violin (Ysaÿe)">Six Sonatas for solo violin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">Dmitri Shostakovich</a> in <a href="/wiki/24_Preludes_and_Fugues_(Shostakovich)" title="24 Preludes and Fugues (Shostakovich)">24 Preludes and Fugues</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heitor_Villa-Lobos" title="Heitor Villa-Lobos">Heitor Villa-Lobos</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Bachianas_Brasileiras" title="Bachianas Brasileiras">Bachianas Brasileiras</a></i>. All kinds of publications involved Bach: not only were there the <i>Bach Jahrbuch</i> publications of the Neue Bachgesellschaft, various other biographies and studies by among others <a href="/wiki/Albert_Schweitzer" title="Albert Schweitzer">Albert Schweitzer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sanford_Terry_(historian)" title="Charles Sanford Terry (historian)">Charles Sanford Terry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_D%C3%BCrr" title="Alfred Dürr">Alfred Dürr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Wolff" title="Christoph Wolff">Christoph Wolff</a>. <a href="/wiki/Peter_Williams_(musicologist)" title="Peter Williams (musicologist)">Peter Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Butt_(musician)" title="John Butt (musician)">John Butt</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[n 5]</a></sup> and the 1950 first edition of the <a href="/wiki/Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis" title="Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis">Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis</a>; but also books such as <i><a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6del,_Escher,_Bach" title="Gödel, Escher, Bach">Gödel, Escher, Bach</a></i> put the composer's art in a wider perspective. Bach's music was extensively listened to, performed, broadcast, arranged, adapted, and commented upon in the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KVNM2000_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-KVNM2000-219">[214]</a></sup> Around 2000, the 250th anniversary of Bach's death, three record companies issued box sets with complete recordings of Bach's music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bach's music features three times—more than that of any other composer—on the <a href="/wiki/Voyager_Golden_Record" title="Voyager Golden Record">Voyager Golden Record</a>, a gramophone record containing a broad sample of the images, common sounds, languages, and music of Earth, sent into outer space with the two <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">Voyager</a> probes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[218]</a></sup> Tributes to Bach in the 20th century include statues erected in his honour and a variety of things such as streets and space objects being named after him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[220]</a></sup> Also, a multitude of musical ensembles such as the <a href="/wiki/Bach_Aria_Group" title="Bach Aria Group">Bach Aria Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bachsolisten" title="Deutsche Bachsolisten">Deutsche Bachsolisten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bachchor_Stuttgart" title="Bachchor Stuttgart">Bachchor Stuttgart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bach_Collegium_Japan" title="Bach Collegium Japan">Bach Collegium Japan</a> adopted the composer's name. <a href="/wiki/Bach_festival" title="Bach festival">Bach festivals</a> were held on several continents, and competitions and prizes such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Johann_Sebastian_Bach_Competition" title="International Johann Sebastian Bach Competition">International Johann Sebastian Bach Competition</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music_Bach_Prize" title="Royal Academy of Music Bach Prize">Royal Academy of Music Bach Prize</a> were named after the composer. While by the end of the 19th century Bach had been inscribed in nationalism and religious revival, the late 20th century saw Bach as the subject of a secularised art-as-religion (<span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Kunstreligion" title="Kunstreligion">Kunstreligion</a></i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay_200-5"><a href="#cite_note-McKay-200">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KVNM2000_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-KVNM2000-219">[214]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3>
<p>In the 21st century, Bach's compositions have become available online, for instance at the <a href="/wiki/International_Music_Score_Library_Project" title="International Music Score Library Project">International Music Score Library Project</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[221]</a></sup> High-resolution facsimiles of Bach's autographs became available at the <a href="/wiki/Bach_Digital" title="Bach Digital">Bach Digital</a> website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[222]</a></sup> 21st-century biographers include <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Wolff" title="Christoph Wolff">Christoph Wolff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Williams_(musicologist)" title="Peter Williams (musicologist)">Peter Williams</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Eliot_Gardiner" title="John Eliot Gardiner">John Eliot Gardiner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[n 6]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Bach's handwritten personal copy of his Mass in B minor, held by the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_State_Library" title="Berlin State Library">Berlin State Library</a>, was added to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme#Memory_of_the_World_Register" title="Memory of the World Programme">Memory of the World Register</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-229">[223]</a></sup> a program intended to protect culturally significant manuscripts.
</p><p>In 2019, Bach was named the greatest composer of all time in a poll conducted among 174 living composers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[224]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burial_site">Burial site</span></h3>
<p>Bach was originally buried at Old St. John's Cemetery in Leipzig. His grave went unmarked for nearly 150 years, but in 1894 his remains were located and moved to a vault in St. John's Church. This building was destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Leipzig_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Leipzig in World War II">Allied bombing during World War II</a>, so in 1950 Bach's remains were taken to their present grave in St. Thomas Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_25-9"><a href="#cite_note-Baroquenet-25">[22]</a></sup> Later research has called into question whether the remains in the grave are actually those of Bach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[225]</a></sup>
</p>
